<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Medicine</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span class="flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."></span><span class="fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" title="show/hide details"></span></div>
<div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails-wrapper" style="position:relative;"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_details" id="mw-fr-revisiondetails" style="display:none">This is the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pending_changes" title="Wikipedia:Pending changes">latest accepted revision</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Medicine">reviewed</a> on <i>5 October 2022</i>.</div>
</div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Diagnosis, treatment, and prevention of illness</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the science  of healing. For medicaments, see <a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">Medication</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Medicine_(disambiguation)" title="Medicine (disambiguation)">Medicine (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox"><caption class="infobox-title" style="padding-bottom:0.25em;">Medicine</caption><tbody><tr><td class="infobox-image" colspan="2"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asklepios.3.jpg"><img alt="Marble statue of Asclephius on a pedestal, symbol of medicine in Western medicine" data-file-height="752" data-file-width="494" decoding="async" height="381" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Asklepios.3.jpg/250px-Asklepios.3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Asklepios.3.jpg/375px-Asklepios.3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Asklepios.3.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a><div class="infobox-caption" style="padding-top:0.25em;padding-bottom:0.4em;">Statue of <a href="/wiki/Asclepius" title="Asclepius">Asclepius</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_God" title="Greek God">Greek god</a> of medicine, holding the symbolic <a href="/wiki/Rod_of_Asclepius" title="Rod of Asclepius">Rod of Asclepius</a> with its coiled <a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">serpent</a></div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-top:0.185em;line-height:1.15em; padding-right:0.5em;">Specialist</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" title="Specialty (medicine)">Medical specialty</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-top:0.185em;line-height:1.15em; padding-right:0.5em;">Glossary</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_medicine" title="Glossary of medicine">Glossary of medicine</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Medicine</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Praxis_(process)" title="Praxis (process)">practice</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> of caring for a patient, managing the <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis" title="Diagnosis">diagnosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prognosis" title="Prognosis">prognosis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_medicine" title="Preventive medicine">prevention</a>, <a href="/wiki/Therapy" title="Therapy">treatment</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Palliative_care" title="Palliative care">palliation</a> of their <a href="/wiki/Injury" title="Injury">injury</a> or <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">disease</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Health_promotion" title="Health promotion">promoting their health</a>. Medicine encompasses a variety of <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> practices evolved to maintain and restore <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prevention_(medical)" title="Prevention (medical)">prevention</a> and <a href="/wiki/Therapy" title="Therapy">treatment</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness" title="Illness">illness</a>. Contemporary medicine applies <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_sciences" title="Biomedical sciences">biomedical sciences</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_research" title="Biomedical research">biomedical research</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medical_genetics" title="Medical genetics">genetics</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_technology" title="Medical technology">medical technology</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diagnosis_(medical)" title="Diagnosis (medical)">diagnose</a>, treat, and prevent injury and disease, typically through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical" title="Pharmaceutical">pharmaceuticals</a> or <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">surgery</a>, but also through therapies as diverse as <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">psychotherapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Splint_(medicine)" title="Splint (medicine)">external splints and traction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medical_device" title="Medical device">medical devices</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biologic_medical_product" title="Biologic medical product">biologics</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiation_(medicine)" title="Radiation (medicine)">ionizing radiation</a>, amongst others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Medicine has been practiced since <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_medicine" title="Prehistoric medicine">prehistoric times</a>, and for most of this time it was an <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> (an area of skill and knowledge), frequently having connections to the <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophical</a> beliefs of local culture. For example, a <a href="/wiki/Medicine_man" title="Medicine man">medicine man</a> would apply <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbs" title="Herbs">herbs</a> and say <a href="/wiki/Prayer" title="Prayer">prayers</a> for healing, or an ancient <a href="/wiki/Philosopher" title="Philosopher">philosopher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a> would apply <a href="/wiki/Bloodletting" title="Bloodletting">bloodletting</a> according to the theories of <a href="/wiki/Humorism" title="Humorism">humorism</a>. In recent centuries, since the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">advent of modern science</a>, most medicine has become a combination of <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> (both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamental_science" title="Fundamental science">basic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied</a>, under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umbrella_term" title="Umbrella term">umbrella</a> of <b>medical science</b>). For example, while stitching technique for <a href="/wiki/Surgical_suture" title="Surgical suture">sutures</a> is an art learned through practice, the knowledge of what happens at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cytology" title="Cytology">cellular</a> and <a href="/wiki/Molecular_medicine" title="Molecular medicine">molecular</a> level in the tissues being stitched arises through science.
</p><p>Prescientific forms of medicine, now known as <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">traditional medicine</a> or <i>folk medicine</i>, remain commonly used in the absence of scientific medicine, and are thus called <a href="/wiki/Alternative_medicine" title="Alternative medicine">alternative medicine</a>. Alternative treatments outside of scientific medicine with safety and efficacy concerns are termed <a href="/wiki/Quackery" title="Quackery">quackery</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Medicine (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-medicine.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-medicine.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/En-us-medicine.ogg" title="En-us-medicine.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>) is the <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> and practice of the <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis" title="Diagnosis">diagnosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prognosis" title="Prognosis">prognosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Therapy" title="Therapy">treatment</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_medicine" title="Preventive medicine">prevention</a> of <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The word "medicine" is derived from <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>medicus</i>, meaning "a physician".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clinical_practice">Clinical practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Clinical practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg"><img alt="Oil painting of medicine in the age of colonialism" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1053" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg/240px-The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg/360px-The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg/480px-The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Doctor_Luke_Fildes_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Doctor</i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Luke_Fildes" title="Sir Luke Fildes">Sir Luke Fildes</a> (1891)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_Blackwell.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="288" decoding="async" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Elizabeth_Blackwell.jpg/220px-Elizabeth_Blackwell.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Elizabeth_Blackwell.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_Blackwell.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Blackwell" title="Elizabeth Blackwell">Elizabeth Blackwell</a>, the first female physician in the United States graduated from <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_Upstate_Medical_University" title="State University of New York Upstate Medical University">SUNY Upstate</a> (1847)</div></div></div>
<p>Medical availability and clinical practice varies across the world due to regional differences in culture and technology. Modern scientific medicine is highly developed in the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>, while in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> such as parts of Africa or Asia, the population may rely more heavily on <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">traditional medicine</a> with limited evidence and efficacy and no required formal training for practitioners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed world</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_medicine" title="Evidence-based medicine">evidence-based medicine</a> is not universally used in clinical practice; for example, a 2007 survey of literature reviews found that about 49% of the interventions lacked sufficient evidence to support either benefit or harm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>In modern clinical practice, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physicians" title="Physicians">physicians</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physician_assistants" title="Physician assistants">physician assistants</a> personally assess patients in order to <a href="/wiki/Medical_diagnosis" title="Medical diagnosis">diagnose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prognosis" title="Prognosis">prognose</a>, treat, and prevent disease using clinical judgment. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor-patient_relationship" title="Doctor-patient relationship">doctor-patient relationship</a> typically begins an interaction with an examination of the patient's <a href="/wiki/Medical_history" title="Medical history">medical history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medical_record" title="Medical record">medical record</a>, followed by a medical interview<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coulehan_2005_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coulehan_2005-10">[10]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">physical examination</a>. Basic diagnostic <a href="/wiki/Medical_device" title="Medical device">medical devices</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Stethoscope" title="Stethoscope">stethoscope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tongue_depressor" title="Tongue depressor">tongue depressor</a>) are typically used. After examination for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_sign" title="Medical sign">signs</a> and interviewing for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symptoms" title="Symptoms">symptoms</a>, the doctor may order <a href="/wiki/Medical_test" title="Medical test">medical tests</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Blood_test" title="Blood test">blood tests</a>), take a <a href="/wiki/Biopsy" title="Biopsy">biopsy</a>, or prescribe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_drug" title="Pharmaceutical drug">pharmaceutical drugs</a> or other therapies. <a href="/wiki/Differential_diagnosis" title="Differential diagnosis">Differential diagnosis</a> methods help to rule out conditions based on the information provided. During the encounter, properly informing the patient of all relevant facts is an important part of the relationship and the development of trust. The medical encounter is then documented in the medical record, which is a legal document in many jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHIMA2005_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-AHIMA2005-11">[11]</a></sup> Follow-ups may be shorter but follow the same general procedure, and specialists follow a similar process. The diagnosis and treatment may take only a few minutes or a few weeks depending upon the complexity of the issue.
</p><p>The components of the medical interview<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coulehan_2005_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Coulehan_2005-10">[10]</a></sup> and encounter are:
</p>
<ul><li>Chief complaint (CC): the reason for the current medical visit. These are the '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symptom" title="Symptom">symptoms</a>.' They are in the patient's own words and are recorded along with the duration of each one. Also called 'chief concern' or 'presenting complaint'.</li>
<li>History of present <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness" title="Illness">illness</a> (HPI): the chronological order of events of symptoms and further clarification of each symptom. Distinguishable from history of previous illness, often called past medical history (PMH). <a href="/wiki/Medical_history" title="Medical history">Medical history</a> comprises HPI and PMH.</li>
<li>Current activity: occupation, hobbies, what the patient actually does.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">Medications</a> (Rx): what drugs the patient takes including <a href="/wiki/Medical_prescription" title="Medical prescription">prescribed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Over-the-counter_drug" title="Over-the-counter drug">over-the-counter</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_remedy" title="Home remedy">home remedies</a>, as well as alternative and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbalism" title="Herbalism">herbal medicines or remedies</a>. <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">Allergies</a> are also recorded.</li>
<li>Past medical history (PMH/PMHx): concurrent medical problems, past hospitalizations and operations, injuries, past <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">infectious diseases</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vaccination" title="Vaccination">vaccinations</a>, history of known allergies.</li>
<li>Social history (SH): birthplace, residences, marital history, social and economic status, habits (including <a href="/wiki/Diet_(nutrition)" title="Diet (nutrition)">diet</a>, medications, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">tobacco</a>, alcohol).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Family_history_(medicine)" title="Family history (medicine)">Family history</a> (FH): listing of diseases in the family that may impact the patient. A <a href="/wiki/Family_tree" title="Family tree">family tree</a> is sometimes used.</li>
<li>Review of systems (ROS) or <i>systems inquiry</i>: a set of additional questions to ask, which may be missed on HPI: a general enquiry (have you noticed any <a href="/wiki/Weight_loss" title="Weight loss">weight loss</a>, change in sleep quality, fevers, lumps and bumps? etc.), followed by questions on the body's main organ systems (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_heart" title="Human heart">heart</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_lung" title="Human lung">lungs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digestive_tract" title="Digestive tract">digestive tract</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urinary_system" title="Urinary system">urinary tract</a>, etc.).</li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">physical examination</a> is the examination of the patient for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_sign" title="Medical sign">medical signs</a> of disease, which are objective and observable, in contrast to symptoms that are volunteered by the patient and not necessarily objectively observable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The healthcare provider uses sight, hearing, touch, and sometimes smell (e.g., in infection, <a href="/wiki/Uremia" title="Uremia">uremia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diabetic_ketoacidosis" title="Diabetic ketoacidosis">diabetic ketoacidosis</a>). Four actions are the basis of physical examination: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inspection_(medicine)" title="Inspection (medicine)">inspection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palpation" title="Palpation">palpation</a> (feel), <a href="/wiki/Percussion_(medicine)" title="Percussion (medicine)">percussion</a> (tap to determine resonance characteristics), and <a href="/wiki/Auscultation" title="Auscultation">auscultation</a> (listen), generally in that order although auscultation occurs prior to percussion and palpation for abdominal assessments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>The clinical examination involves the study of:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Vital signs including height, weight, body temperature, <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulse" title="Pulse">pulse</a>, respiration rate, and hemoglobin <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_saturation" title="Oxygen saturation">oxygen saturation</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li>General appearance of the patient and specific indicators of disease (nutritional status, presence of jaundice, pallor or <a href="/wiki/Nail_clubbing" title="Nail clubbing">clubbing</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Human_skin" title="Human skin">Skin</a></li>
<li>Head, <a href="/wiki/Eye" title="Eye">eye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ear" title="Ear">ear</a>, nose, and throat (<a href="/wiki/HEENT_examination" title="HEENT examination">HEENT</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiovascular" title="Cardiovascular">Cardiovascular</a> (<a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blood_vessel" title="Blood vessel">blood vessels</a>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory" title="Respiratory">Respiratory</a> (large airways and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_lung" title="Human lung">lungs</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Abdomen" title="Abdomen">Abdomen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rectum" title="Rectum">rectum</a></li>
<li>Genitalia (and pregnancy if the patient is or could be pregnant)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musculoskeletal" title="Musculoskeletal">Musculoskeletal</a> (including spine and extremities)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neurological" title="Neurological">Neurological</a> (consciousness, awareness, brain, vision, <a href="/wiki/Cranial_nerves" title="Cranial nerves">cranial nerves</a>, spinal cord and <a href="/wiki/Peripheral_nervous_system" title="Peripheral nervous system">peripheral nerves</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">Psychiatric</a> (orientation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_state_examination" title="Mental state examination">mental state</a>, mood, evidence of abnormal perception or thought).</li></ul>
<p>It is to likely focus on areas of interest highlighted in the medical history and may not include everything listed above.
</p><p>The treatment plan may include ordering additional <a href="/wiki/Medical_laboratory" title="Medical laboratory">medical laboratory</a> tests and <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">medical imaging</a> studies, starting therapy, referral to a specialist, or watchful observation. Follow-up may be advised. Depending upon the <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a> plan and the <a href="/wiki/Managed_care" title="Managed care">managed care</a> system, various forms of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utilization_review" title="Utilization review">utilization review</a>", such as prior authorization of tests, may place barriers on accessing expensive services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The medical decision-making (MDM) process involves analysis and synthesis of all the above data to come up with a list of possible diagnoses (the <a href="/wiki/Differential_diagnosis" title="Differential diagnosis">differential diagnoses</a>), along with an idea of what needs to be done to obtain a definitive diagnosis that would explain the patient's problem.
</p><p>On subsequent visits, the process may be repeated in an abbreviated manner to obtain any new history, symptoms, physical findings, and lab or imaging results or specialist consultations.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions">Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg"><img alt="Color fresco of an ancient hospital setting" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1460" data-file-width="1820" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg/220px-Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg/330px-Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg/440px-Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pellegrinaio_Santa_Maria_della_Scala_n5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Hospital of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_della_Scala_(Siena)" title="Santa Maria della Scala (Siena)">Santa Maria della Scala</a>, fresco by <a href="/wiki/Domenico_di_Bartolo" title="Domenico di Bartolo">Domenico di Bartolo</a>, 1441–1442</div></div></div>
<p>Contemporary medicine is in general conducted within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_system" title="Health care system">health care systems</a>. Legal, <a href="/wiki/Credential" title="Credential">credentialing</a> and financing frameworks are established by individual governments, augmented on occasion by international organizations, such as churches. The characteristics of any given health care system have significant impact on the way medical care is provided.
</p><p>From ancient times, Christian emphasis on practical charity gave rise to the development of systematic nursing and hospitals and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> today remains the largest non-government provider of medical services in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Advanced industrial countries (with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOM_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-IOM-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccuhc_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccuhc-18">[18]</a></sup> and many <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> provide medical services through a system of <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> that aims to guarantee care for all through a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single-payer_health_care" title="Single-payer health care">single-payer health care</a> system, or compulsory private or co-operative <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>. This is intended to ensure that the entire population has access to medical care on the basis of need rather than ability to pay. Delivery may be via private medical practices or by state-owned hospitals and clinics, or by charities, most commonly by a combination of all three.
</p><p>Most <a href="/wiki/Tribe" title="Tribe">tribal</a> societies provide no guarantee of healthcare for the population as a whole. In such societies, healthcare is available to those that can afford to pay for it or have self-insured it (either directly or as part of an employment contract) or who may be covered by care financed by the government or tribe directly.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg"><img alt="collection of glass bottles of different sizes" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3040" data-file-width="2214" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg/170px-Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg/255px-Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg/340px-Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drug_ampoule_JPN.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern drug <a href="/wiki/Ampoule" title="Ampoule">ampoules</a></div></div></div>
<p>Transparency of information is another factor defining a delivery system. Access to information on conditions, treatments, quality, and pricing greatly affects the choice by patients/consumers and, therefore, the incentives of medical professionals. While the US healthcare system has come under fire for lack of openness,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> new legislation may encourage greater openness. There is a perceived tension between the need for transparency on the one hand and such issues as patient confidentiality and the possible exploitation of information for commercial gain on the other.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Health_professional" title="Health professional">health professionals</a> who provide care in medicine comprise multiple <a href="/wiki/Profession" title="Profession">professions</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">medics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nurses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_therapy" title="Physical therapy">physio therapists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Psychologist" title="Psychologist">psychologists</a>. These professions will have their own <a href="/wiki/Professional_ethics" title="Professional ethics">ethical standards</a>, professional education, and bodies. The medical profession have been conceptualized from a <a href="/wiki/Medical_sociology#The_Medical_Profession" title="Medical sociology">sociological perspective</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Delivery">Delivery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Delivery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">Health care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clinic" title="Clinic">clinic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">hospital</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hospice" title="Hospice">hospice</a></div>
<p>Provision of medical care is classified into primary, secondary, and tertiary care categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic,_PNG_(10711159465).jpg"><img alt="photograph of three nurses" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="682" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic%2C_PNG_%2810711159465%29.jpg/170px-Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic%2C_PNG_%2810711159465%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic%2C_PNG_%2810711159465%29.jpg/255px-Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic%2C_PNG_%2810711159465%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic%2C_PNG_%2810711159465%29.jpg/340px-Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic%2C_PNG_%2810711159465%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nurses_at_Butawin_Urban_Clinic,_PNG_(10711159465).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nurses in <a href="/wiki/Kokopo" title="Kokopo">Kokopo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_New_Britain" title="East New Britain">East New Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">Primary care</a> medical services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physician_assistant" title="Physician assistant">physician assistants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nurse_practitioner" title="Nurse practitioner">nurse practitioners</a>, or other health professionals who have first contact with a patient seeking medical treatment or care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> These occur in physician offices, <a href="/wiki/Clinic" title="Clinic">clinics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nursing_home" title="Nursing home">nursing homes</a>, schools, home visits, and other places close to patients. About 90% of medical visits can be treated by the primary care provider. These include treatment of acute and chronic illnesses, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_care" title="Preventive care">preventive care</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_education" title="Health education">health education</a> for all ages and both sexes.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_care" title="Secondary care">Secondary care</a> medical services are provided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_specialist" title="Medical specialist">medical specialists</a> in their offices or clinics or at local community hospitals for a patient referred by a primary care provider who first diagnosed or treated the patient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Referrals are made for those patients who required the expertise or procedures performed by specialists. These include both <a href="/wiki/Ambulatory_care" title="Ambulatory care">ambulatory care</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inpatient" title="Inpatient">inpatient</a> services, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">Emergency departments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intensive_care_medicine" title="Intensive care medicine">intensive care medicine</a>, surgery services, <a href="/wiki/Physical_therapy" title="Physical therapy">physical therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Childbirth" title="Childbirth">labor and delivery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endoscopy" title="Endoscopy">endoscopy</a> units, diagnostic <a href="/wiki/Medical_laboratory" title="Medical laboratory">laboratory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">medical imaging</a> services, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hospice_care" title="Hospice care">hospice</a> centers, etc. Some primary care providers may also take care of hospitalized patients and deliver babies in a secondary care setting.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_care" title="Tertiary care">Tertiary care</a> medical services are provided by specialist hospitals or regional centers equipped with diagnostic and treatment facilities not generally available at local hospitals. These include <a href="/wiki/Trauma_center" title="Trauma center">trauma centers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burn_(injury)" title="Burn (injury)">burn</a> treatment centers, advanced <a href="/wiki/Neonatology" title="Neonatology">neonatology</a> unit services, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" title="Organ transplant">organ transplants</a>, high-risk pregnancy, <a href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy" title="Radiation therapy">radiation</a> <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">oncology</a>, etc.
</p><p>Modern medical care also depends on information – still delivered in many health care settings on paper records, but increasingly nowadays by <a href="/wiki/Electronic_health_record" title="Electronic health record">electronic means</a>.
</p><p>In low-income countries, modern healthcare is often too expensive for the average person. International healthcare policy researchers have advocated that "user fees" be removed in these areas to ensure access, although even after removal, significant costs and barriers remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Separation_of_prescribing_and_dispensing" title="Separation of prescribing and dispensing">Separation of prescribing and dispensing</a> is a practice in medicine and pharmacy in which the <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a> who provides a <a href="/wiki/Medical_prescription" title="Medical prescription">medical prescription</a> is independent from the  <a href="/wiki/Pharmacist" title="Pharmacist">pharmacist</a> who provides the <a href="/wiki/Prescription_drug" title="Prescription drug">prescription drug</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> there are centuries of tradition for separating pharmacists from physicians. In Asian countries, it is traditional for physicians to also provide drugs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Branches">Branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies,_1918.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1941" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies%2C_1918.jpg/220px-Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies%2C_1918.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies%2C_1918.jpg/330px-Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies%2C_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies%2C_1918.jpg/440px-Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies%2C_1918.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drawing_by_Marguerite_Martyn_of_a_visiting_nurse_with_medicine_and_four_babies,_1918.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drawing by <a href="/wiki/Marguerite_Martyn" title="Marguerite Martyn">Marguerite Martyn</a> (1918) of a visiting nurse in St. Louis, Missouri, with medicine and babies</div></div></div>
<p>Working together as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interdisciplinary_team" title="Interdisciplinary team">interdisciplinary team</a>, many highly trained <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_profession" title="Health profession">health professionals</a> besides medical practitioners are involved in the delivery of modern health care. Examples include: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse" title="Nurse">nurses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_medical_technician" title="Emergency medical technician">emergency medical technicians</a> and paramedics, laboratory scientists, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmacists" title="Pharmacists">pharmacists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Podiatry" title="Podiatry">podiatrists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physiotherapists" title="Physiotherapists">physiotherapists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_therapists" title="Respiratory therapists">respiratory therapists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_therapy" title="Speech therapy">speech therapists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occupational_therapy" title="Occupational therapy">occupational therapists</a>, radiographers, <a href="/wiki/Dietitian" title="Dietitian">dietitians</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bioengineering" title="Bioengineering">bioengineers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medical_physics" title="Medical physics">medical physics</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surgeons" title="Surgeons">surgeons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surgeon%27s_assistant" title="Surgeon's assistant">surgeon's assistant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surgical_technologist" title="Surgical technologist">surgical technologist</a>.
</p><p>The scope and sciences underpinning human medicine overlap many other fields. <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">Dentistry</a>, while considered by some a separate discipline from medicine, is a medical field.
</p><p>A patient admitted to the hospital is usually under the care of a specific team based on their main presenting problem, e.g., the cardiology team, who then may interact with other specialties, e.g., surgical, radiology, to help diagnose or treat the main problem or any subsequent complications/developments.
</p><p>Physicians have many specializations and subspecializations into certain branches of medicine, which are listed below. There are variations from country to country regarding which specialties certain subspecialties are in.
</p><p>The main branches of medicine are:
</p>
<ul><li>Basic sciences of medicine; this is what every physician is educated in, and some return to in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_research#Preclinical_research" title="Biomedical research">biomedical research</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_specialties" title="Medical specialties">Medical specialties</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interdisciplinary_sub-specialties_of_medicine" title="Interdisciplinary sub-specialties of medicine">Interdisciplinary fields</a>, where different medical specialties are mixed to function in certain occasions.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_sciences">Basic sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Basic sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">Anatomy</a></i> is the study of the physical structure of <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a>. In contrast to <i>macroscopic</i> or <i>gross anatomy</i>, <i>cytology</i> and <i>histology</i> are concerned with microscopic structures.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">Biochemistry</a></i> is the study of the chemistry taking place in living organisms, especially the structure and function of their chemical components.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Biomechanics" title="Biomechanics">Biomechanics</a></i> is the study of the structure and function of biological systems by means of the methods of <a href="/wiki/Mechanics" title="Mechanics">Mechanics</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Biostatistics" title="Biostatistics">Biostatistics</a></i> is the application of statistics to biological fields in the broadest sense. A knowledge of biostatistics is essential in the planning, evaluation, and interpretation of medical research. It is also fundamental to <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">epidemiology</a> and evidence-based medicine.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">Biophysics</a></i> is an interdisciplinary science that uses the methods of <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physical_chemistry" title="Physical chemistry">physical chemistry</a> to study biological systems.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">Cytology</a></i> is the microscopic study of individual <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a>.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2532" data-file-width="2082" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg/220px-Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg/330px-Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg/440px-Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Edelfelt_-_Louis_Pasteur_-_1885.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur" title="Louis Pasteur">Louis Pasteur</a></i>, as portrayed in his laboratory, 1885 by <a href="/wiki/Albert_Edelfelt" title="Albert Edelfelt">Albert Edelfelt</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Embryology" title="Embryology">Embryology</a></i> is the study of the early development of organisms.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Endocrinology" title="Endocrinology">Endocrinology</a></i> is the study of hormones and their effect throughout the body of animals.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</a></i> is the study of the demographics of disease processes, and includes, but is not limited to, the study of epidemics.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">Genetics</a></i> is the study of genes, and their role in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_inheritance" title="Biological inheritance">biological inheritance</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Histology" title="Histology">Histology</a></i> is the study of the structures of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_tissue" title="Biological tissue">biological tissues</a> by light <a href="/wiki/Microscopy" title="Microscopy">microscopy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electron_microscope" title="Electron microscope">electron microscopy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immunohistochemistry" title="Immunohistochemistry">immunohistochemistry</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Immunology" title="Immunology">Immunology</a></i> is the study of the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a>, which includes the innate and adaptive immune system in humans, for example.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lifestyle_medicine" title="Lifestyle medicine">Lifestyle medicine</a></i> is the study of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chronic_conditions" title="Chronic conditions">chronic conditions</a>, and how to prevent, treat and reverse them.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Medical_physics" title="Medical physics">Medical physics</a></i> is the study of the applications of physics principles in medicine.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Microbiology" title="Microbiology">Microbiology</a></i> is the study of <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">bacteria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">Molecular biology</a></i> is the study of molecular underpinnings of the process of <a href="/wiki/DNA_replication" title="DNA replication">replication</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcription_(genetics)" title="Transcription (genetics)">transcription</a> and <a href="/wiki/Translation_(biology)" title="Translation (biology)">translation</a> of the genetic material.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">Neuroscience</a></i> includes those disciplines of science that are related to the study of the <a href="/wiki/Nervous_system" title="Nervous system">nervous system</a>. A main focus of neuroscience is the <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> and physiology of the human brain and <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord" title="Spinal cord">spinal cord</a>. Some related clinical specialties include <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">neurology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">neurosurgery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">psychiatry</a>.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nutrition_science" title="Nutrition science">Nutrition science</a></i> (theoretical focus) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dietetics" title="Dietetics">dietetics</a></i> (practical focus) is the study of the relationship of food and drink to health and disease, especially in determining an optimal diet. Medical nutrition therapy is done by dietitians and is prescribed for <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular diseases</a>, weight and eating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_illness" title="Mental illness">disorders</a>, allergies, <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoplasia" title="Neoplasia">neoplastic</a> diseases.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathology_as_a_science" title="Pathology as a science">Pathology as a science</a></i> is the study of disease—the causes, course, progression and resolution thereof.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pharmacology" title="Pharmacology">Pharmacology</a></i> is the study of drugs and their actions.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gynecology" title="Gynecology">Gynecology</a></i> is the study of female reproductive system.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Photobiology" title="Photobiology">Photobiology</a></i> is the study of the interactions between <a href="/wiki/Non-ionizing_radiation" title="Non-ionizing radiation">non-ionizing radiation</a> and living organisms.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">Physiology</a></i> is the study of the normal functioning of the body and the underlying regulatory mechanisms.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Radiobiology" title="Radiobiology">Radiobiology</a></i> is the study of the interactions between <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">ionizing radiation</a> and living organisms.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Toxicology" title="Toxicology">Toxicology</a></i> is the study of hazardous effects of drugs and <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poisons</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialties">Specialties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Specialties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">Medical specialty</a></div>
<p>In the broadest meaning of "medicine", there are many different specialties. In the UK, most specialities have their own body or college, which has its own entrance examination. These are collectively known as the Royal Colleges, although not all currently use the term "Royal". The development of a speciality is often driven by new technology (such as the development of effective anaesthetics) or ways of working (such as emergency departments); the new specialty leads to the formation of a unifying body of doctors and the prestige of administering their own examination.
</p><p>Within medical circles, specialities usually fit into one of two broad categories: "Medicine" and "Surgery". "Medicine" refers to the practice of non-operative medicine, and most of its subspecialties require preliminary training in Internal Medicine. In the UK, this was traditionally evidenced by passing the examination for the Membership of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Physicians" title="Royal College of Physicians">Royal College of Physicians</a> (MRCP) or the equivalent college in Scotland or Ireland. "Surgery" refers to the practice of operative medicine, and most subspecialties in this area require preliminary training in General Surgery, which in the UK leads to membership of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Surgeons_of_England" title="Royal College of Surgeons of England">Royal College of Surgeons of England</a> (MRCS). At present, some specialties of medicine do not fit easily into either of these categories, such as radiology, pathology, or anesthesia. Most of these have branched from one or other of the two camps above; for example anaesthesia developed first as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faculty_(teaching_staff)" title="Faculty (teaching staff)">faculty</a> of the Royal College of Surgeons (for which MRCS/FRCS would have been required) before becoming the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Anaesthetists" title="Royal College of Anaesthetists">Royal College of Anaesthetists</a> and membership of the college is attained by sitting for the examination of the Fellowship of the Royal College of Anesthetists (FRCA).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Surgical_specialty">Surgical specialty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Surgical specialty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">Surgery</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surgeons_at_Work.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Surgeons_at_Work.jpg/220px-Surgeons_at_Work.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Surgeons_at_Work.jpg/330px-Surgeons_at_Work.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Surgeons_at_Work.jpg/440px-Surgeons_at_Work.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surgeons_at_Work.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Surgeons in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operating_room" title="Operating room">operating room</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Surgery</b> is an ancient medical specialty that uses operative manual and instrumental techniques on a patient to investigate or treat a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathological" title="Pathological">pathological</a> condition such as <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">disease</a> or <a href="/wiki/Injury" title="Injury">injury</a>, to help improve bodily function or appearance or to repair unwanted ruptured areas (for example, <a href="/wiki/Perforated_eardrum" title="Perforated eardrum">a perforated ear drum</a>). Surgeons must also manage pre-operative, post-operative, and potential surgical candidates on the hospital wards. In some centers, <a href="/wiki/Anesthesiology" title="Anesthesiology">anesthesiology</a> is part of the division of surgery (for historical and logistical reasons), although it is not a surgical discipline. Other medical specialties may employ surgical procedures, such as <a href="/wiki/Ophthalmology" title="Ophthalmology">ophthalmology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dermatology" title="Dermatology">dermatology</a>, but are not considered surgical sub-specialties per se.
</p><p>Surgical training in the U.S. requires a minimum of five years of residency after medical school. Sub-specialties of surgery often require seven or more years. In addition, fellowships can last an additional one to three years. Because post-residency fellowships can be competitive, many trainees devote two additional years to research. Thus in some cases surgical training will not finish until more than a decade after medical school. Furthermore, surgical training can be very difficult and time-consuming.
</p><p>Surgical subspecialties include those a physician may specialize in after undergoing general surgery residency training as well as several surgical fields with separate residency training. Surgical subspecialties that one may pursue following general surgery residency training: <i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-26">[26]</a></sup></i>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/General_surgery" title="General surgery">General surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bariatric_surgery" title="Bariatric surgery">Bariatric surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cardiac_surgery" title="Cardiac surgery">Cardiovascular surgery</a> - may also be pursued through a separate cardiovascular surgery residency track</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorectal_surgery" title="Colorectal surgery">Colorectal surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Endocrine_surgery" title="Endocrine surgery">Endocrine surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hand_surgery" title="Hand surgery">Hand surgery</a></li>
<li>Hepatico-Pancreatico-Biliary Surgery</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minimally-invasive_surgery" title="Minimally-invasive surgery">Minimally invasive surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Surgical_oncology" title="Surgical oncology">Surgical oncology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pediatric_surgery" title="Pediatric surgery">Pediatric surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Plastic_surgery" title="Plastic surgery">Plastic surgery</a> - may also be pursued through a separate plastic surgery residency track</li>
<li>Surgical critical care</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Organ_transplantation" title="Organ transplantation">Transplant surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trauma_surgery" title="Trauma surgery">Trauma surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vascular_surgery" title="Vascular surgery">Vascular surgery</a> - may also be pursued through a separate vascular surgery residency track</li></ul>
<p>Other surgical specialties within medicine with their own individual residency training:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dermatology" title="Dermatology">Dermatology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">Neurosurgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ophthalmology" title="Ophthalmology">Ophthalmology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oral_and_maxillofacial_surgery" title="Oral and maxillofacial surgery">Oral and Maxillofacial surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orthopedic_surgery" title="Orthopedic surgery">Orthopedic surgery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otorhinolaryngology" title="Otorhinolaryngology">Otorhinolaryngology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Podiatry" title="Podiatry">Podiatric surgery</a> - do not undergo medical school training, but rather separate training in podiatry school</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Urology" title="Urology">Urology</a></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_medicine_specialty">Internal medicine specialty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Internal medicine specialty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Internal_medicine" title="Internal medicine">Internal medicine</a></div>
<p><b>Internal medicine</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">medical specialty</a> dealing with the prevention, diagnosis, and treatment of adult diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> According to some sources, an emphasis on internal structures is implied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In North America, specialists in internal medicine are commonly called "internists". Elsewhere, especially in <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> nations, such specialists are often called <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fowler_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler-29">[29]</a></sup> These terms, <i>internist</i> or <i>physician</i> (in the narrow sense, common outside North America), generally exclude practitioners of gynecology and obstetrics, pathology, psychiatry, and especially surgery and its subspecialities.
</p><p>Because their patients are often seriously ill or require complex investigations, internists do much of their work in hospitals. Formerly, many internists were not subspecialized; such <i>general physicians</i> would see any complex nonsurgical problem; this style of practice has become much less common. In modern urban practice, most internists are subspecialists: that is, they generally limit their medical practice to problems of one organ system or to one particular area of medical knowledge. For example, <a href="/wiki/Gastroenterology" title="Gastroenterology">gastroenterologists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nephrology" title="Nephrology">nephrologists</a> specialize respectively in diseases of the gut and the kidneys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and some other countries, specialist <a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">pediatricians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geriatrics" title="Geriatrics">geriatricians</a> are also described as <i>specialist physicians</i> (or internists) who have subspecialized by age of patient rather than by organ system. Elsewhere, especially in North America, general pediatrics is often a form of <a href="/wiki/Primary_care_physician" title="Primary care physician">primary care</a>.
</p><p>There are many subspecialities (or subdisciplines) of <a href="/wiki/Internal_medicine" title="Internal medicine">internal medicine</a>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1054258005">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents ul,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents ul li{list-style:none}@media(max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li{padding-left:1.6em;text-indent:-1.6em}}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="refbegin refbegin-columns references-column-count references-column-count-3" style="column-count: 3;">
<dl><dd><ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Angiology" title="Angiology">Angiology</a>/Vascular Medicine</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bariatrics" title="Bariatrics">Bariatrics</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Cardiology" title="Cardiology">Cardiology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critical_care_medicine" title="Critical care medicine">Critical care medicine</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Endocrinology" title="Endocrinology">Endocrinology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Gastroenterology" title="Gastroenterology">Gastroenterology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Geriatrics" title="Geriatrics">Geriatrics</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hematology" title="Hematology">Hematology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hepatology" title="Hepatology">Hepatology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease_(medical_specialty)" title="Infectious disease (medical specialty)">Infectious disease</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Nephrology" title="Nephrology">Nephrology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">Neurology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">Oncology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">Pediatrics</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pulmonology" title="Pulmonology">Pulmonology</a>/Pneumology/Respirology/chest medicine</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Rheumatology" title="Rheumatology">Rheumatology</a></i></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_Medicine" title="Sports Medicine">Sports Medicine</a></i></li></ul></dd></dl></div>
<p>Training in internal medicine (as opposed to surgical training), varies considerably across the world: see the articles on <i><a href="/wiki/Medical_education" title="Medical education">medical education</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a></i> for more details. In North America, it requires at least three years of residency training after medical school, which can then be followed by a one- to three-year fellowship in the subspecialties listed above. In general, resident work hours in medicine are less than those in surgery, averaging about 60 hours per week in the US. This difference does not apply in the UK where all doctors are now required by law to work less than 48 hours per week on average.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnostic_specialties">Diagnostic specialties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Diagnostic specialties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinical_laboratory" title="Clinical laboratory">Clinical laboratory</a> sciences</i> are the clinical diagnostic services that apply laboratory techniques to diagnosis and management of patients. In the United States, these services are supervised by a pathologist. The personnel that work in these <a href="/wiki/Medical_laboratory" title="Medical laboratory">medical laboratory</a> departments are technically trained staff who do not hold medical degrees, but who usually hold an undergraduate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_technology" title="Medical technology">medical technology</a> degree, who actually perform the <a href="/wiki/Medical_test" title="Medical test">tests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assay" title="Assay">assays</a>, and procedures needed for providing the specific services. Subspecialties include <a href="/wiki/Transfusion_medicine" title="Transfusion medicine">transfusion medicine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellular_pathology" title="Cellular pathology">cellular pathology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clinical_chemistry" title="Clinical chemistry">clinical chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hematology" title="Hematology">hematology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinical_microbiology" title="Clinical microbiology">clinical microbiology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinical_immunology" title="Clinical immunology">clinical immunology</a>.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathology_as_a_medical_specialty" title="Pathology as a medical specialty">Pathology as a medical specialty</a></i> is the branch of medicine that deals with the study of diseases and the morphologic, physiologic changes produced by them. As a diagnostic specialty, pathology can be considered the basis of modern scientific medical knowledge and plays a large role in <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_medicine" title="Evidence-based medicine">evidence-based medicine</a>. Many modern molecular tests such as <a href="/wiki/Flow_cytometry" title="Flow cytometry">flow cytometry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polymerase_chain_reaction" title="Polymerase chain reaction">polymerase chain reaction</a> (PCR), <a href="/wiki/Immunohistochemistry" title="Immunohistochemistry">immunohistochemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cytogenetics" title="Cytogenetics">cytogenetics</a>, gene rearrangements studies and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluorescent_in_situ_hybridization" title="Fluorescent in situ hybridization">fluorescent in situ hybridization</a> (FISH) fall within the territory of pathology.</li>
<li><i>Diagnostic <a href="/wiki/Radiology" title="Radiology">radiology</a></i> is concerned with imaging of the body, e.g. by <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">x-rays</a>, x-ray <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computed_tomography" title="Computed tomography">computed tomography</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultrasonography" title="Ultrasonography">ultrasonography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_magnetic_resonance" title="Nuclear magnetic resonance">nuclear magnetic resonance</a> <a href="/wiki/Tomography" title="Tomography">tomography</a>. Interventional radiologists can access areas in the body under imaging for an intervention or diagnostic sampling.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_medicine" title="Nuclear medicine">Nuclear medicine</a></i> is concerned with studying human organ systems by administering radiolabelled substances (radiopharmaceuticals) to the body, which can then be imaged outside the body by a <a href="/wiki/Gamma_camera" title="Gamma camera">gamma camera</a> or a PET scanner. Each radiopharmaceutical consists of two parts: a tracer that is specific for the function under study (e.g., neurotransmitter pathway, metabolic pathway, blood flow, or other), and a radionuclide (usually either a gamma-emitter or a positron emitter). There is a degree of overlap between nuclear medicine and radiology, as evidenced by the emergence of combined devices such as the PET/CT scanner.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Clinical_neurophysiology" title="Clinical neurophysiology">Clinical neurophysiology</a></i> is concerned with testing the physiology or function of the central and peripheral aspects of the nervous system. These kinds of tests can be divided into recordings of: (1) spontaneous or continuously running electrical activity, or (2) stimulus evoked responses. Subspecialties include <a href="/wiki/Electroencephalography" title="Electroencephalography">electroencephalography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electromyography" title="Electromyography">electromyography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evoked_potential" title="Evoked potential">evoked potential</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nerve_conduction_study" title="Nerve conduction study">nerve conduction study</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polysomnography" title="Polysomnography">polysomnography</a>. Sometimes these tests are performed by techs without a medical degree, but the interpretation of these tests is done by a medical professional.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_major_specialties">Other major specialties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other major specialties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The following are some major medical specialties that do not directly fit into any of the above-mentioned groups:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Anesthesiology" title="Anesthesiology">Anesthesiology</a></i> (also known as <i>anaesthetics</i>): concerned with the perioperative management of the surgical patient. The anesthesiologist's role during surgery is to prevent derangement in the vital organs' (i.e. brain, heart, kidneys) functions and postoperative pain. Outside of the operating room, the anesthesiology physician also serves the same function in the labor and delivery ward, and some are specialized in critical medicine.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Emergency_medicine" title="Emergency medicine">Emergency medicine</a></i> is concerned with the diagnosis and treatment of acute or life-threatening conditions, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_trauma" title="Physical trauma">trauma</a>, surgical, medical, pediatric, and psychiatric emergencies.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Family_medicine" title="Family medicine">Family medicine</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_practice" title="Family practice">family practice</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/General_practice" title="General practice">general practice</a></i> or <i>primary care</i> is, in many countries, the first port-of-call for patients with non-emergency medical problems. Family physicians often provide services across a broad range of settings including office based practices, emergency department coverage, inpatient care, and nursing home care.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_(12330467294).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_%2812330467294%29.jpg/220px-Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_%2812330467294%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_%2812330467294%29.jpg/330px-Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_%2812330467294%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_%2812330467294%29.jpg/440px-Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_%2812330467294%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Changing_lives_for_girls_and_women_every_week_(12330467294).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gynecologist" title="Gynecologist">Gynecologist</a> Michel Akotionga of <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Obstetrics" title="Obstetrics">Obstetrics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gynecology" title="Gynecology">gynecology</a></i> (often abbreviated as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OB/GYN" title="OB/GYN">OB/GYN</a></i> (American English) or <i>Obs &amp; Gynae</i> (British English)) are concerned respectively with childbirth and the female reproductive and associated organs. <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_medicine" title="Reproductive medicine">Reproductive medicine</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_medicine" title="Fertility medicine">fertility medicine</a> are generally practiced by gynecological specialists.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Medical_genetics" title="Medical genetics">Medical genetics</a></i> is concerned with the diagnosis and management of hereditary disorders.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">Neurology</a></i> is concerned with diseases of the nervous system. In the UK, neurology is a subspecialty of general medicine.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">Pediatrics</a></i> (AE) or <i>paediatrics</i> (BE) is devoted to the care of infants, children, and adolescents. Like internal medicine, there are many pediatric subspecialties for specific age ranges, organ systems, disease classes, and sites of care delivery.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_medicine" title="Pharmaceutical medicine">Pharmaceutical medicine</a></i> is the medical scientific discipline concerned with the discovery, development, evaluation, registration, monitoring and medical aspects of marketing of medicines for the benefit of patients and public health.</li>
