<li><i><a href="/wiki/Physical_medicine_and_rehabilitation" title="Physical medicine and rehabilitation">Physical medicine and rehabilitation</a></i> (or <i>physiatry</i>) is concerned with functional improvement after injury, illness, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congenital_disorder" title="Congenital disorder">congenital disorders</a>.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Podiatric_medicine" title="Podiatric medicine">Podiatric medicine</a></i> is the study of, diagnosis, and medical &amp; surgical treatment of disorders of the foot, ankle, lower limb, hip and lower back.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">Psychiatry</a></i> is the branch of medicine concerned with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biopsychosocial" title="Biopsychosocial">bio-psycho-social</a> study of the <a href="/wiki/Etiology" title="Etiology">etiology</a>, diagnosis, treatment and prevention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognitive" title="Cognitive">cognitive</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perceptual" title="Perceptual">perceptual</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emotional" title="Emotional">emotional</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Behavioral" title="Behavioral">behavioral</a> disorders. Related fields include <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">psychotherapy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clinical_psychology" title="Clinical psychology">clinical psychology</a>.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_medicine" title="Preventive medicine">Preventive medicine</a></i> is the branch of medicine concerned with preventing disease.
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Community_health" title="Community health">Community health</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a></i> is an aspect of health services concerned with threats to the overall health of a community based on <a href="/wiki/Population_health" title="Population health">population health</a> analysis.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interdisciplinary_fields">Interdisciplinary fields</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Interdisciplinary fields">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some interdisciplinary sub-specialties of medicine include:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerospace_medicine" title="Aerospace medicine">Aerospace medicine</a></i> deals with medical problems related to flying and <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">space travel</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Addiction_medicine" title="Addiction medicine">Addiction medicine</a></i> deals with the treatment of addiction.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Medical_ethics" title="Medical ethics">Medical ethics</a></i> deals with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethic" title="Ethic">ethical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moral" title="Moral">moral</a> principles that apply values and judgments to the practice of medicine.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_Engineering" title="Biomedical Engineering">Biomedical Engineering</a></i> is a field dealing with the application of <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> principles to medical practice.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Clinical_pharmacology" title="Clinical pharmacology">Clinical pharmacology</a></i> is concerned with how systems of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Therapeutics" title="Therapeutics">therapeutics</a> interact with patients.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Conservation_medicine" title="Conservation medicine">Conservation medicine</a></i> studies the relationship between human and animal health, and environmental conditions. Also known as ecological medicine, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_medicine" title="Environmental medicine">environmental medicine</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Medical_geology" title="Medical geology">medical geology</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Disaster_medicine" title="Disaster medicine">Disaster medicine</a></i> deals with medical aspects of emergency preparedness, disaster mitigation and management.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Diving_medicine" title="Diving medicine">Diving medicine</a></i> (or <a href="/wiki/Hyperbaric_medicine" title="Hyperbaric medicine">hyperbaric medicine</a>) is the prevention and treatment of diving-related problems.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_medicine" title="Evolutionary medicine">Evolutionary medicine</a></i> is a perspective on medicine derived through applying <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolutionary theory</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Forensic_medicine" title="Forensic medicine">Forensic medicine</a></i> deals with medical questions in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal" title="Legal">legal</a> context, such as determination of the time and cause of death, type of weapon used to inflict trauma, reconstruction of the facial features using remains of deceased (skull) thus aiding identification.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gender-based_medicine" title="Gender-based medicine">Gender-based medicine</a></i> studies the biological and physiological differences between the human sexes and how that affects differences in disease.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hospice_and_Palliative_Medicine" title="Hospice and Palliative Medicine">Hospice and Palliative Medicine</a></i> is a relatively modern branch of clinical medicine that deals with pain and symptom relief and emotional support in patients with <a href="/wiki/Terminal_illness" title="Terminal illness">terminal illnesses</a> including cancer and <a href="/wiki/Heart_failure" title="Heart failure">heart failure</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hospital_medicine" title="Hospital medicine">Hospital medicine</a></i> is the general medical care of hospitalized patients. Physicians whose primary professional focus is hospital medicine are called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hospitalist" title="Hospitalist">hospitalists</a> in the United States and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The term Most Responsible Physician (MRP) or attending physician is also used interchangeably to describe this role.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Laser_medicine" title="Laser medicine">Laser medicine</a></i> involves the use of lasers in the diagnostics or treatment of various conditions.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Medical_humanities" title="Medical humanities">Medical humanities</a></i> includes the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> (<a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">ethics</a>, history and religion), <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social science</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cultural_studies" title="Cultural studies">cultural studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a>), and the arts (<a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, theater, film, and <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts" title="Visual arts">visual arts</a>) and their application to <a href="/wiki/Medical_education" title="Medical education">medical education</a> and practice.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Health_informatics" title="Health informatics">Health informatics</a></i> is a relatively recent field that deal with the application of computers and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a> to medicine.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Nosology" title="Nosology">Nosology</a></i> is the classification of diseases for various purposes.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Nosokinetics" title="Nosokinetics">Nosokinetics</a></i> is the science/subject of measuring and modelling the process of care in health and social care systems.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Occupational_medicine" title="Occupational medicine">Occupational medicine</a></i> is the provision of health advice to organizations and individuals to ensure that the highest standards of health and safety at work can be achieved and maintained.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pain_management" title="Pain management">Pain management</a></i> (also called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pain_medicine" title="Pain medicine">pain medicine</a></i>, or <i>algiatry</i>) is the medical discipline concerned with the relief of pain.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pharmacogenomics" title="Pharmacogenomics">Pharmacogenomics</a></i> is a form of <i>individualized medicine</i>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Podiatry" title="Podiatry">Podiatric medicine</a></i> is the study of, diagnosis, and medical treatment of disorders of the foot, ankle, lower limb, hip and lower back.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Sexual_medicine" title="Sexual medicine">Sexual medicine</a></i> is concerned with diagnosing, assessing and treating all disorders related to sexuality.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Sports_medicine" title="Sports medicine">Sports medicine</a></i> deals with the treatment and prevention and rehabilitation of sports/exercise injuries such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle_spasm" title="Muscle spasm">muscle spasms</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle_tear" title="Muscle tear">muscle tears</a>, injuries to ligaments (ligament tears or ruptures) and their repair in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportsperson" title="Sportsperson">athletes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amateur" title="Amateur">amateur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional" title="Professional">professional</a>.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Therapeutics" title="Therapeutics">Therapeutics</a></i> is the field, more commonly referenced in earlier periods of history, of the various remedies that can be used to treat disease and promote health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Travel_medicine" title="Travel medicine">Travel medicine</a></i> or <i>emporiatrics</i> deals with health problems of international travelers or travelers across highly different environments.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Tropical_medicine" title="Tropical medicine">Tropical medicine</a></i> deals with the prevention and treatment of tropical diseases. It is studied separately in temperate climates where those diseases are quite unfamiliar to medical practitioners and their local clinical needs.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urgent_care" title="Urgent care">Urgent care</a></i> focuses on delivery of unscheduled, walk-in care outside of the hospital emergency department for injuries and illnesses that are not severe enough to require care in an emergency department. In some jurisdictions this function is combined with the emergency department.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Veterinary_medicine" title="Veterinary medicine">Veterinary medicine</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veterinarians" title="Veterinarians">veterinarians</a> apply similar techniques as physicians to the care of animals.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilderness_medicine_(practice)" title="Wilderness medicine (practice)">Wilderness medicine</a></i> entails the practice of medicine in the wild, where conventional medical facilities may not be available.</li>
<li>Many other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_science" title="Health science">health science</a> fields, e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dietetics" title="Dietetics">dietetics</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_legal_controls">Education and legal controls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education and legal controls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Medical_education" title="Medical education">Medical education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medical_license" title="Medical license">Medical license</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_(2760577402).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1968" data-file-width="2932" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_%282760577402%29.jpg/220px-Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_%282760577402%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_%282760577402%29.jpg/330px-Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_%282760577402%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_%282760577402%29.jpg/440px-Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_%282760577402%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medical_students_learning_about_stitches_(2760577402).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Medical students learning about stitches</div></div></div>
<p>Medical education and training varies around the world. It typically involves entry level education at a university <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a>, followed by a period of supervised practice or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_intern" title="Medical intern">internship</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Residency_(medicine)" title="Residency (medicine)">residency</a>. This can be followed by postgraduate vocational training. A variety of teaching methods have been employed in medical education, still itself a focus of active research. In Canada and the United States of America, a <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">Doctor of Medicine</a> degree, often abbreviated M.D., or a <a href="/wiki/Osteopathic_medicine_in_the_United_States" title="Osteopathic medicine in the United States">Doctor of Osteopathic Medicine</a> degree, often abbreviated as D.O. and unique to the United States, must be completed in and delivered from a recognized university.
</p><p>Since knowledge, techniques, and medical technology continue to evolve at a rapid rate, many regulatory authorities require <a href="/wiki/Continuing_medical_education" title="Continuing medical education">continuing medical education</a>. Medical practitioners upgrade their knowledge in various ways, including <a href="/wiki/Medical_journal" title="Medical journal">medical journals</a>, seminars, conferences, and online programs.  A database of objectives covering medical knowledge, as suggested by national societies across the United States, can be searched at <a class="external free" href="http://data.medobjectives.marian.edu/" rel="nofollow">http://data.medobjectives.marian.edu/</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medObjectives_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-medObjectives-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madrid_(RPS_13-07-2010)_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a,_fachada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1994" data-file-width="1720" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Madrid_%28RPS_13-07-2010%29_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_fachada.jpg/180px-Madrid_%28RPS_13-07-2010%29_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_fachada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Madrid_%28RPS_13-07-2010%29_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_fachada.jpg/270px-Madrid_%28RPS_13-07-2010%29_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_fachada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Madrid_%28RPS_13-07-2010%29_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_fachada.jpg/360px-Madrid_%28RPS_13-07-2010%29_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_fachada.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madrid_(RPS_13-07-2010)_Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a,_fachada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Organizaci%C3%B3n_M%C3%A9dica_Colegial_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Organización Médica Colegial de España">Organización Médica Colegial de España</a>, which regulates the medical profession in Spain</div></div></div>
<p>In most countries, it is a legal requirement for a medical doctor to be licensed or registered. In general, this entails a medical degree from a university and accreditation by a medical board or an equivalent national organization, which may ask the applicant to pass exams. This restricts the considerable legal authority of the medical profession to physicians that are trained and qualified by national standards. It is also intended as an assurance to patients and as a safeguard against <a href="/wiki/Charlatan" title="Charlatan">charlatans</a> that practice inadequate medicine for personal gain. While the laws generally require medical doctors to be trained in "evidence based", Western, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippocratic" title="Hippocratic">Hippocratic</a> Medicine, they are not intended to discourage different paradigms of health.
</p><p>In the European Union, the profession of doctor of medicine is regulated. A profession is said to be regulated when access and exercise is subject to the possession of a specific professional qualification.
The regulated professions database contains a list of regulated professions for doctor of medicine in the EU member states, EEA countries and Switzerland. This list is covered by the Directive 2005/36/EC.
</p><p>Doctors who are negligent or intentionally harmful in their care of patients can face charges of <a href="/wiki/Medical_malpractice" title="Medical malpractice">medical malpractice</a> and be subject to civil, criminal, or professional sanctions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_ethics">Medical ethics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Medical ethics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medical_ethics" title="Medical ethics">Medical ethics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HippocraticOath.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="983" data-file-width="696" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/HippocraticOath.jpg/170px-HippocraticOath.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/HippocraticOath.jpg/255px-HippocraticOath.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/HippocraticOath.jpg/340px-HippocraticOath.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HippocraticOath.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 12th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_empire" title="Byzantine empire">Byzantine</a> manuscript of the <a href="/wiki/Hippocratic_Oath" title="Hippocratic Oath">Hippocratic Oath</a></div></div></div>
<p>Medical ethics is a system of moral principles that apply values and judgments to the practice of medicine. As a scholarly discipline, medical ethics encompasses its practical application in clinical settings as well as work on its history, philosophy, theology, and sociology. Six of the values that commonly apply to medical ethics discussions are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Autonomy#Medicine" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a> – the patient has the right to refuse or choose their treatment. (<i>Voluntas aegroti suprema lex</i>.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beneficence_(ethics)" title="Beneficence (ethics)">beneficence</a> – a practitioner should act in the best interest of the patient. (<i>Salus aegroti suprema lex</i>.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Justice_(ethics)" title="Justice (ethics)">justice</a> – concerns the distribution of scarce health resources, and the decision of who gets what treatment (fairness and equality).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Primum_non_nocere" title="Primum non nocere">non-maleficence</a> – "first, do no harm" (<i>primum non-nocere</i>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Respect_for_persons" title="Respect for persons">respect for persons</a> – the patient (and the person treating the patient) have the right to be treated with dignity.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Truth" title="Truth">truthfulness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honesty" title="Honesty">honesty</a> – the concept of <a href="/wiki/Informed_consent" title="Informed consent">informed consent</a> has increased in importance since the historical events of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctors%27_Trial" title="Doctors' Trial">Doctors' Trial</a> of the Nuremberg trials, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuskegee_syphilis_experiment" title="Tuskegee syphilis experiment">Tuskegee syphilis experiment</a>, and others.</li></ul>
<p>Values such as these do not give answers as to how to handle a particular situation, but provide a useful framework for understanding conflicts. When moral values are in conflict, the result may be an ethical <a href="/wiki/Dilemma" title="Dilemma">dilemma</a> or crisis. Sometimes, no good solution to a dilemma in medical ethics exists, and occasionally, the values of the medical community (i.e., the hospital and its staff) conflict with the values of the individual patient, family, or larger non-medical community. Conflicts can also arise between health care providers, or among family members. For example, some argue that the principles of autonomy and beneficence clash when patients refuse <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_transfusions" title="Blood transfusions">blood transfusions</a>, considering them life-saving; and truth-telling was not emphasized to a large extent before the HIV era.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_medicine" title="History of medicine">History of medicine</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_medicine_and_medical_technology" title="Timeline of medicine and medical technology">Timeline of medicine and medical technology</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Imhotep-Louvre.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Imhotep-Louvre.JPG/170px-Imhotep-Louvre.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Imhotep-Louvre.JPG/255px-Imhotep-Louvre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Imhotep-Louvre.JPG/340px-Imhotep-Louvre.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Imhotep-Louvre.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statuette of ancient Egyptian physician <a href="/wiki/Imhotep" title="Imhotep">Imhotep</a>, the first physician from antiquity known by name</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_world">Ancient world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ancient world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_medicine" title="Prehistoric medicine">Prehistoric medicine</a> incorporated plants (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbalism" title="Herbalism">herbalism</a>), animal parts, and minerals. In many cases these materials were used ritually as magical substances by priests, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shamans" title="Shamans">shamans</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Medicine_man" title="Medicine man">medicine men</a>. Well-known spiritual systems include <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a> (the notion of inanimate objects having spirits), <a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">spiritualism</a> (an appeal to gods or communion with ancestor spirits); <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">shamanism</a> (the vesting of an individual with mystic powers); and <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> (magically obtaining the truth). The field of <a href="/wiki/Medical_anthropology" title="Medical anthropology">medical anthropology</a> examines the ways in which culture and society are organized around or impacted by issues of health, health care and related issues.
</p><p>Early records on medicine have been discovered from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egyptian_medicine" title="Ancient Egyptian medicine">ancient Egyptian medicine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonian_Medicine" title="Babylonian Medicine">Babylonian Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayurveda" title="Ayurveda">Ayurvedic</a> medicine (in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Chinese_medicine" title="Classical Chinese medicine">classical Chinese medicine</a> (predecessor to the modern <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_medicine" title="Traditional Chinese medicine">traditional Chinese medicine</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_medicine" title="Ancient Greek medicine">ancient Greek medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicine_in_ancient_Rome" title="Medicine in ancient Rome">Roman medicine</a>.
</p><p>In Egypt, <a href="/wiki/Imhotep" title="Imhotep">Imhotep</a> (3rd millennium BCE) is the first physician in history known by name. The oldest <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_medical_papyri" title="Egyptian medical papyri">Egyptian medical text</a> is the <i><a href="/wiki/Kahun_Gynaecological_Papyrus" title="Kahun Gynaecological Papyrus">Kahun Gynaecological Papyrus</a></i> from around 2000 BCE, which describes gynaecological diseases. The <i><a href="/wiki/Edwin_Smith_Papyrus" title="Edwin Smith Papyrus">Edwin Smith Papyrus</a></i> dating back to 1600 BCE is an early work on surgery, while the <i><a href="/wiki/Ebers_Papyrus" title="Ebers Papyrus">Ebers Papyrus</a></i> dating back to 1500 BCE is akin to a textbook on medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Acker_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Acker-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>In China, archaeological evidence of medicine in Chinese dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shang_Dynasty" title="Shang Dynasty">Shang Dynasty</a>, based on seeds for herbalism and tools presumed to have been used for surgery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Huangdi_Neijing" title="Huangdi Neijing">Huangdi Neijing</a></i>, the progenitor of Chinese medicine, is a medical text written beginning in the 2nd century BCE and compiled in the 3rd century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unsc_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unsc-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>In India, the surgeon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sushruta" title="Sushruta">Sushruta</a> described numerous surgical operations, including the earliest forms of <a href="/wiki/Plastic_surgery" title="Plastic surgery">plastic surgery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Singh-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (July 2010)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Medicine#Dubious" title="Talk:Medicine">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Longfellow_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Longfellow-37">[37]</a></sup> Earliest records of dedicated hospitals come from Mihintale in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> where evidence of dedicated medicinal treatment facilities for patients are found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="495" decoding="async" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg/240px-HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg/360px-HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg/480px-HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HSAsclepiusKos_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mosaic on the floor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asclepieion" title="Asclepieion">Asclepieion</a> of Kos, depicting <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a>, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asklepius" title="Asklepius">Asklepius</a> in the middle (2nd–3rd century)</div></div></div>
<p>In Greece, the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_medicine" title="Ancient Greek medicine">Greek physician</a> <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a>, the "father of modern medicine",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18392218_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18392218-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackwellpublishing.com_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-blackwellpublishing.com-41">[41]</a></sup> laid the foundation for a rational approach to medicine. Hippocrates introduced the <a href="/wiki/Hippocratic_Oath" title="Hippocratic Oath">Hippocratic Oath</a> for physicians, which is still relevant and in use today, and was the first to categorize illnesses as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acute_(medical)" title="Acute (medical)">acute</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chronic_(medicine)" title="Chronic (medicine)">chronic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endemic_(epidemiology)" title="Endemic (epidemiology)">endemic</a> and epidemic, and use terms such as, "exacerbation, <a href="/wiki/Relapse" title="Relapse">relapse</a>, resolution, crisis, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paroxysm" title="Paroxysm">paroxysm</a>, peak, and <a href="/wiki/Convalescence" title="Convalescence">convalescence</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-garrison97_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-garrison97-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mart90_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-mart90-43">[43]</a></sup> The Greek physician <a href="/wiki/Galen" title="Galen">Galen</a> was also one of the greatest surgeons of the ancient world and performed many audacious operations, including brain and eye surgeries. After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> and the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a>, the Greek tradition of medicine went into decline in Western Europe, although it continued uninterrupted in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman (Byzantine) Empire</a>.
</p><p>Most of our knowledge of ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew_medicine" title="Hebrew medicine">Hebrew medicine</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1st_millennium_BC" title="1st millennium BC">1st millennium BC</a> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a>, i.e. the Five Books of <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a>, which contain various health related laws and rituals. The Hebrew contribution to the development of modern medicine started in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_Era" title="Byzantine Era">Byzantine Era</a>, with the physician <a href="/wiki/Asaph_the_Jew" title="Asaph the Jew">Asaph the Jew</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="348" decoding="async" height="374" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG/220px-Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG/330px-Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A manuscript of <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Risalah_al-Dhahabiah" title="Al-Risalah al-Dhahabiah">Al-Risalah al-Dhahabiah</a></i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ali_al-Ridha" title="Ali al-Ridha">Ali al-Ridha</a>, the eighth Imam of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twelver" title="Twelver">Shia Muslims</a>. The text says: "Golden dissertation in medicine which is sent by Imam Ali ibn Musa al-Ridha, peace be upon him, to <a href="/wiki/Al-Ma%27mun" title="Al-Ma'mun">al-Ma'mun</a>."</div></div></div>
<p>The concept of hospital as institution to offer medical care and possibility of a cure for the patients due to the ideals of Christian charity, rather than just merely a place to die, appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the concept of <a href="/wiki/Uroscopy" title="Uroscopy">uroscopy</a> was known to Galen, he did not see the importance of using it to localize the disease. It was under the Byzantines with physicians such of <a href="/wiki/Theophilus_Protospatharius" title="Theophilus Protospatharius">Theophilus Protospatharius</a> that they realized the potential in uroscopy to determine disease in a time when no microscope or stethoscope existed. That practice eventually spread to the rest of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>After 750 CE, the Muslim world had the works of Hippocrates, Galen and Sushruta translated into <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_medicine" title="Islamic medicine">Islamic physicians</a> engaged in some significant medical research. Notable Islamic medical pioneers include the <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persian</a> <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a>, who, along with Imhotep and Hippocrates, has also been called the "father of medicine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> He wrote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Canon_of_Medicine" title="The Canon of Medicine">The Canon of Medicine</a></i> which became a standard medical text at many medieval European <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">universities</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> considered one of the most famous books in the history of medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Others include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_al-Qasim_al-Zahrawi" title="Abu al-Qasim al-Zahrawi">Abulcasis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Zuhr" title="Ibn Zuhr">Avenzoar</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rabie2006_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rabie2006-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Nafis" title="Ibn al-Nafis">Ibn al-Nafis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Averroes" title="Averroes">Averroes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Persian  physician <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Zakar%C4%ABya_R%C4%81zi" title="Muhammad ibn Zakarīya Rāzi">Rhazes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tschanz_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tschanz-54">[54]</a></sup> was one of the first to question the Greek theory of <a href="/wiki/Humorism" title="Humorism">humorism</a>, which nevertheless remained influential in both medieval Western and medieval <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_medicine" title="Islamic medicine">Islamic medicine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Some volumes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Zakar%C4%ABya_R%C4%81zi" title="Muhammad ibn Zakarīya Rāzi">Rhazes</a>'s work <i>Al-Mansuri</i>, namely "On Surgery" and "A General Book on Therapy", became part of the medical curriculum in European universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Additionally, he has been described as a doctor's doctor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> the father of <a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">pediatrics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tschanz_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tschanz-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elgood_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elgood-58">[58]</a></sup> and a pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Ophthalmology" title="Ophthalmology">ophthalmology</a>. For example, he was the first to recognize the reaction of the eye's pupil to light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elgood_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elgood-58">[58]</a></sup> The Persian <a href="/wiki/Bimaristan" title="Bimaristan">Bimaristan</a> hospitals were an early example of <a href="/wiki/Public_hospital" title="Public hospital">public hospitals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrett_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barrett-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Europe, <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> decreed that a hospital should be attached to each cathedral and monastery and the historian <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Blainey" title="Geoffrey Blainey">Geoffrey Blainey</a> likened the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_and_health_care" title="Catholic Church and health care">activities of the Catholic Church in health care</a> during the Middle Ages to an early version of a welfare state: "It conducted hospitals for the old and orphanages for the young; hospices for the sick of all ages; places for the lepers; and hostels or inns where pilgrims could buy a cheap bed and meal". It supplied food to the population during famine and distributed food to the poor. This welfare system the church funded through collecting taxes on a large scale and possessing large farmlands and estates. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictine" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> order was noted for setting up hospitals and infirmaries in their monasteries, growing medical herbs and becoming the chief medical care givers of their districts, as at the great <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbey_of_Cluny" title="Abbey of Cluny">Abbey of Cluny</a>. The Church also established a network of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_schools" title="Cathedral schools">cathedral schools</a> and universities where medicine was studied. The <a href="/wiki/Schola_Medica_Salernitana" title="Schola Medica Salernitana">Schola Medica Salernitana</a> in Salerno, looking to the learning of <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arab</a> physicians, grew to be the finest medical school in Medieval Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG/260px-SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG/390px-SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG/520px-SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SantaMariaDellaScalaSienaBack.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Siena's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_della_Scala_(Siena)" title="Santa Maria della Scala (Siena)">Santa Maria della Scala Hospital</a>, one of Europe's oldest hospitals. During the Middle Ages, the Catholic Church established universities to revive the study of sciences, drawing on the learning of Greek and Arab physicians in the study of medicine.</div></div></div>
<p>However, the fourteenth and fifteenth century <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> devastated both the Middle East and Europe, and it has even been argued that Western Europe was generally more effective in recovering from the pandemic than the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In the early modern period, important early figures in medicine and anatomy emerged in Europe, including <a href="/wiki/Gabriele_Falloppio" title="Gabriele Falloppio">Gabriele Falloppio</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Harvey" title="William Harvey">William Harvey</a>.
</p><p>The major shift in medical thinking was the gradual rejection, especially during the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> in the 14th and 15th centuries, of what may be called the "traditional authority" approach to science and medicine. This was the notion that because some prominent person in the past said something must be so, then that was the way it was, and anything one observed to the contrary was an anomaly (which was paralleled by a similar shift in European society in general – see <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Copernicus</a>'s rejection of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>'s theories on astronomy). Physicians like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vesalius" title="Vesalius">Vesalius</a> improved upon or disproved some of the theories from the past. The main tomes used both by medicine students and expert physicians were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Materia_Medica" title="Materia Medica">Materia Medica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pharmacopoeia" title="Pharmacopoeia">Pharmacopoeia</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Andreas_Vesalius" title="Andreas Vesalius">Andreas Vesalius</a> was the author of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_humani_corporis_fabrica" title="De humani corporis fabrica">De humani corporis fabrica</a></i>, an important book on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_anatomy" title="Human anatomy">human anatomy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Bacteria and microorganisms were first observed with a microscope by <a href="/wiki/Antonie_van_Leeuwenhoek" title="Antonie van Leeuwenhoek">Antonie van Leeuwenhoek</a> in 1676, initiating the scientific field <a href="/wiki/Microbiology" title="Microbiology">microbiology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brock_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brock-64">[64]</a></sup> Independently from <a href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Nafis" title="Ibn al-Nafis">Ibn al-Nafis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Servetus" title="Michael Servetus">Michael Servetus</a> rediscovered the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a>, but this discovery did not reach the public because it was written down for the first time in the "Manuscript of Paris"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> in 1546, and later published in the theological work for which he paid with his life in 1553. Later this was described by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renaldus_Columbus" title="Renaldus Columbus">Renaldus Columbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Cesalpino" title="Andrea Cesalpino">Andrea Cesalpino</a>. <a href="/wiki/Herman_Boerhaave" title="Herman Boerhaave">Herman Boerhaave</a> is sometimes referred to as a "father of physiology" due to his exemplary teaching in Leiden and textbook 'Institutiones medicae' (1708). <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Fauchard" title="Pierre Fauchard">Pierre Fauchard</a> has been called "the father of modern dentistry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="358" data-file-width="488" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg/220px-Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg/330px-Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg/440px-Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul-Louis_Simond_injecting_plague_vaccine_June_4th_1898_Karachi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paul-Louis_Simond" title="Paul-Louis Simond">Paul-Louis Simond</a> injecting a plague vaccine in <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>, 1898</div></div></div>
<p>Veterinary medicine was, for the first time, truly separated from human medicine in 1761, when the French veterinarian <a href="/wiki/Claude_Bourgelat" title="Claude Bourgelat">Claude Bourgelat</a> founded the world's first veterinary school in Lyon, France. Before this, medical doctors treated both humans and other animals.
</p><p>Modern scientific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_research" title="Biomedical research">biomedical research</a> (where results are testable and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reproducible" title="Reproducible">reproducible</a>) began to replace early Western traditions based on herbalism, the Greek "<a href="/wiki/Humorism" title="Humorism">four humours</a>" and other such pre-modern notions. The modern era really began with <a href="/wiki/Edward_Jenner" title="Edward Jenner">Edward Jenner</a>'s discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Smallpox_vaccine" title="Smallpox vaccine">smallpox vaccine</a> at the end of the 18th century (inspired by the method of <a href="/wiki/Inoculation" title="Inoculation">inoculation</a> earlier practiced in Asia), <a href="/wiki/Robert_Koch" title="Robert Koch">Robert Koch</a>'s discoveries around 1880 of the transmission of disease by bacteria, and then the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotics</a> around 1900.
</p><p>The post-18th century <a href="/wiki/Modernity" title="Modernity">modernity</a> period brought more groundbreaking researchers from Europe. From <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and Austria, doctors <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Virchow" title="Rudolf Virchow">Rudolf Virchow</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Conrad_R%C3%B6ntgen" title="Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen">Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Landsteiner" title="Karl Landsteiner">Karl Landsteiner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otto_Loewi" title="Otto Loewi">Otto Loewi</a> made notable contributions. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Fleming" title="Alexander Fleming">Alexander Fleming</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Lister,_1st_Baron_Lister" title="Joseph Lister, 1st Baron Lister">Joseph Lister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick" title="Francis Crick">Francis Crick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a> are considered important. <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> doctor <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal" title="Santiago Ramón y Cajal">Santiago Ramón y Cajal</a> is considered the father of modern <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a>.
</p><p>From New Zealand and Australia came <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Wilkins" title="Maurice Wilkins">Maurice Wilkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Florey" title="Howard Florey">Howard Florey</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frank_Macfarlane_Burnet" title="Frank Macfarlane Burnet">Frank Macfarlane Burnet</a>.
</p><p>Others that did significant work include <a href="/wiki/William_Williams_Keen" title="William Williams Keen">William Williams Keen</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Coley" title="William Coley">William Coley</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_D._Watson" title="James D. Watson">James D. Watson</a> (United States); <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Luria" title="Salvador Luria">Salvador Luria</a> (Italy); <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Yersin" title="Alexandre Yersin">Alexandre Yersin</a> (Switzerland); <a href="/wiki/Kitasato_Shibasabur%C5%8D" title="Kitasato Shibasaburō">Kitasato Shibasaburō</a> (Japan); <a href="/wiki/Jean-Martin_Charcot" title="Jean-Martin Charcot">Jean-Martin Charcot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Bernard" title="Claude Bernard">Claude Bernard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Broca" title="Paul Broca">Paul Broca</a> (France); <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Lutz" title="Adolfo Lutz">Adolfo Lutz</a> (Brazil); <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Korotkov" title="Nikolai Korotkov">Nikolai Korotkov</a> (Russia); <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">Sir William Osler</a> (Canada); and <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Cushing" title="Harvey Cushing">Harvey Cushing</a> (United States).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Fleming.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="385" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Alexander_Fleming.jpg/220px-Alexander_Fleming.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Alexander_Fleming.jpg/330px-Alexander_Fleming.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Alexander_Fleming.jpg/440px-Alexander_Fleming.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Fleming.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Fleming" title="Alexander Fleming">Alexander Fleming</a>'s discovery of penicillin in September 1928 marks the start of modern antibiotics.</div></div></div>
<p>As science and technology developed, medicine became more reliant upon <a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">medications</a>. Throughout history and in Europe right until the late 18th century, not only animal and plant products were used as medicine, but also human body parts and fluids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pharmacology" title="Pharmacology">Pharmacology</a> developed in part from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbalism" title="Herbalism">herbalism</a> and some drugs are still derived from plants (<a href="/wiki/Atropine" title="Atropine">atropine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ephedrine" title="Ephedrine">ephedrine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warfarin" title="Warfarin">warfarin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aspirin" title="Aspirin">aspirin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digoxin" title="Digoxin">digoxin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinca_alkaloid" title="Vinca alkaloid"><i>vinca</i> alkaloids</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxo" title="Taxo">taxol</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyoscine_hydrobromide" title="Hyoscine hydrobromide">hyoscine</a>, etc.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vaccine" title="Vaccine">Vaccines</a> were discovered by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Jenner" title="Edward Jenner">Edward Jenner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur" title="Louis Pasteur">Louis Pasteur</a>.
</p><p>The first antibiotic was <a href="/wiki/Arsphenamine" title="Arsphenamine">arsphenamine</a> (Salvarsan) discovered by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ehrlich" title="Paul Ehrlich">Paul Ehrlich</a> in 1908 after he observed that bacteria took up toxic dyes that human cells did not. The first major class of <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotics</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Sulfonamide_(medicine)" title="Sulfonamide (medicine)">sulfa drugs</a>, derived by German chemists originally from <a href="/wiki/Azo_dye" title="Azo dye">azo dyes</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._(16248845637).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3204" data-file-width="2506" decoding="async" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._%2816248845637%29.jpg/220px-Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._%2816248845637%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._%2816248845637%29.jpg/330px-Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._%2816248845637%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._%2816248845637%29.jpg/440px-Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._%2816248845637%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Syd%C3%A4nl%C3%A4%C3%A4kkeen_pakkausta_l%C3%A4%C3%A4ketehdas_Starilla_vuonna_1953._Kuva_Vapriikin_kuva-arkisto._(16248845637).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Packaging of <a href="/wiki/Cardiology" title="Cardiology">cardiac medicine</a> at the Star pharmaceutical factory in <a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> in 1953.</div></div></div>
<p>Pharmacology has become increasingly sophisticated; modern <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> allows drugs targeted towards specific physiological processes to be developed, sometimes designed for compatibility with the body to reduce <a href="/wiki/Side_effect" title="Side effect">side-effects</a>. <a href="/wiki/Genomics" title="Genomics">Genomics</a> and knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Human_genetics" title="Human genetics">human genetics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_evolution" title="Human evolution">human evolution</a> is having increasingly significant influence on medicine, as the causative <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> of most monogenic <a href="/wiki/Genetic_disorder" title="Genetic disorder">genetic disorders</a> have now been identified, and the development of techniques in <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a> are influencing medical technology, practice and decision-making.
</p><p>Evidence-based medicine is a contemporary movement to establish the most effective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algorithms" title="Algorithms">algorithms</a> of practice (ways of doing things) through the use of <a href="/wiki/Systematic_review" title="Systematic review">systematic reviews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">meta-analysis</a>. The movement is facilitated by modern global <a href="/wiki/Information_science" title="Information science">information science</a>, which allows as much of the available evidence as possible to be collected and analyzed according to standard protocols that are then disseminated to healthcare providers. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochrane_Collaboration" title="Cochrane Collaboration">Cochrane Collaboration</a> leads this movement. A 2001 review of 160 Cochrane systematic reviews revealed that, according to two readers, 21.3% of the reviews concluded insufficient evidence, 20% concluded evidence of no effect, and 22.5% concluded positive effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ezzo2001_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ezzo2001-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Quality.2C_efficiency.2C_and_access"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Quality,_efficiency,_and_access">Quality, efficiency, and access</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Quality, efficiency, and access">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_medicine" title="Evidence-based medicine">Evidence-based medicine</a>, prevention of <a href="/wiki/Medical_error" title="Medical error">medical error</a> (and other "<a href="/wiki/Iatrogenesis" title="Iatrogenesis">iatrogenesis</a>"), and avoidance of <a href="/wiki/Unnecessary_health_care" title="Unnecessary health care">unnecessary health care</a> are a priority in modern medical systems. These topics generate significant political and public policy attention, particularly in the United States where healthcare is regarded as excessively costly but <a href="/wiki/Population_health" title="Population health">population health</a> metrics lag similar nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>Globally, many <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> lack access to care and <a href="/wiki/Access_to_medicines" title="Access to medicines">access to medicines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> As of 2015, most wealthy developed countries provide <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">health care to all citizens</a>, with a few exceptions such as the United States where lack of <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a> coverage may limit access.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Etymology: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">medicina</i>, from <i>ars medicina</i> "the medical art", from <i>medicus</i> "physician". (<a class="external text" href="http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=medicine" rel="nofollow">Etym.Online</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071011122928/http://etymonline.com/index.php?term=medicine" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 11 October 2007 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>) Cf. <i>mederi</i> "to heal", etym. "know the best course for", from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">PIE</a> base *med- "to measure, limit. Cf. <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>medos</i> "counsel, plan", <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avestan_language" title="Avestan language">Avestan</a> <i>vi-mad</i> "physician"</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Michael Dols has shown that the Black Death was much more commonly believed by European authorities than by Middle Eastern authorities to be contagious; as a result, flight was more commonly counseled, and in urban Italy quarantines were organized on a much wider level than in urban Egypt or Syria (<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFDols1977">Dols MW (1977). <i>The Black Death in the Middle East</i>.
